## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations & dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables position x and velocity v evolving in time t, matching second-order oscillator ODEs (often written as x'' = dv_dt = f(x,v,t)). Nonlinear harmonic oscillator models typically combine a restoring force depending on x, damping depending on v, and possibly external/parametric forcing depending on t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-normalized spring + dashpot)
- Time-varying damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation)
- Pendulum/sine restoring nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations, odd restoring force)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (softening/hardening spring, conservative form)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness with linear damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (dissipation proportional to speed squared)
- Nonlinear (Rayleigh-type) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * v**2) * v (damping increases with speed)
- van der Pol (Liénard) oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * (x**2 - c2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Driven damped oscillator (external forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance under forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type stiffness modulation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (parametric resonance regions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically yield dv_dt depending only on x (no v term); adding v-terms introduces dissipation or self-excitation.
- Odd symmetry in x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3, -sin(x)) corresponds to symmetric potentials U(x) and oscillations centered at x = 0.
- Cubic stiffness terms (x**3) indicate amplitude-dependent natural frequency (hardening/softening), often seen as nonlinear resonance shifts.
- Terms like v*Abs(v) or v**3 represent drag-like losses that grow strongly with speed, producing faster decay at large amplitudes than linear damping.
- Negative damping at small amplitude but positive damping at large amplitude (e.g., -(x**2 - c)*v) is a signature mechanism for stable limit cycles (self-sustained oscillations).
- Explicit sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) additions indicate external periodic forcing; responses may show resonance, subharmonics, and hysteresis when combined with nonlinearity.
- Time-periodic modulation multiplying x (parametric excitation) suggests Mathieu-type instability tongues and parametric resonance near twice the natural frequency.
- If dv_dt includes products like x*v (or x**2*v), it often encodes state-dependent damping or energy transfer that depends on phase (position–velocity).
